Miss William's Letter to Wu Dingchang Praising China's Anti-War Movement

Since the establishment of the Anti-Civil War League, not only the Chinese people have unanimously supported it, but also people from friendly countries have sincerely assisted it. Recently, Miss William from the United States sent a letter to Chairman Wu of the Anti-War League, saying, "Mr. Wu Dingchang, I have received your letter of July 5 with respect. At that time, Mr. Davis happened to be in this country, so I immediately sent a copy of your esteemed letter to Mr. Davis. I am delighted to know that your country's Anti-Civil War League believes that our country's Goodwill Committee can be expected to help it proceed in the future. We sincerely hope that you all also know that we deeply admire the organization and nature of your association. Our country's Goodwill Committee is extremely honored to be able to fully cooperate with China's patriotic groups. I am also pleased to read that your association's work is progressing day by day. Your association's slogan is 'China must not have another civil war,' which is not only a blessing for China but also a blessing for the whole world. Today's scholars all know that the key to the peace and prosperity of the world today lies entirely in China. To seek China's unification, peace, and stability, there must be a national construction plan, and the success of this plan depends heavily on the assistance of industrialized countries. Therefore, countries that cooperate with China will share the benefits of its revitalization with China. Therefore, the American Goodwill Committee deeply hopes that after coming to China, it can further express the American people's desire for your association's success and enhance the relationship between China and the United States. Moreover, China and the United States must have a closer economic relationship for their own benefit. China's great mass consumption capacity and the United States' great mass production capacity are naturally matched. Based on the experience of the past four years, our country knows that mass production without corresponding mass consumption is more dangerous than mass consumption without corresponding mass production. This shows that our desire for Sino-American cooperation is truly for the common political and economic interests of both countries. Therefore, your association's ability to bring peace and unification to China is equally beneficial to both China and the United States and can serve as a preliminary step for international cooperation. I am pleased to hear that President Liu Zhan'en of Shanghai University will soon come to the United States and represent your association to discuss progress with the American Goodwill Committee. We deeply know that Mr. Liu will definitely cooperate successfully with our association. We look forward to his arrival with great joy. I know that you will send me your esteemed book 'Commentary on the Three Principles of the People.' When I have the opportunity to read it, I will definitely gain a lot. I hereby respectfully wish you success in your patriotic efforts and look forward to cooperating with you with great pleasure. Sincerely, William, August 14, 1933, from New York."

Du Yuesheng and Others Initiate the Pudong Wind Disaster Relief Association Established Yesterday

－Scheduled to Petition Finance Minister Song and the Jiangsu Provincial Government－

The recent hurricane that swept through Shanghai caused particularly severe damage in Pudong, Chuansha, Nanhui, and other areas. The disaster-stricken people are in urgent need of help. Gentry and merchants from these areas asked Mr. Du Yuesheng and other prominent figures in Shanghai to find ways to provide relief. Mr. Du and others specially formed the "Shanghai Pudong Wind and Tide Disaster Relief Committee," which was officially established yesterday. They are scheduled to petition Finance Minister Song for funds and the Jiangsu Provincial Government. The details are recorded as follows:

(Representatives Present) Those present yesterday included Xu Shiying (represented by Huang Bodu), Wang Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng, Wang Yiting (represented by Huang Hanzhi), Lu Wenshao, Li Zicai, Yu Zuoting (represented by Gao Jijing), Zou Bingwen, Wen Lanting, Wang Yansong, Yang Qingyuan, Pang Hanzhi, Chen Songyuan, Hu Bijang (represented by Xu Jianwu), Chen Zixin, Gu Wensheng, Xu Xinliu, Shi Liangcai, Zhang Bochou, Feng Bingnan, Lu Bohong, Huang Renzhi, Yuan Ludeng, Yuan Xiluo, Gui Yanfang, Guan Jiongzhi, Lin Kanghou, Zheng Hongnian, Wu Yunzhai, and over a hundred others, chaired by Du Yuesheng.

(Chairman's Report) After the meeting opened with formalities, Chairman Du Yuesheng first reported on the disaster situation, saying, "On the evenings of the 2nd and 18th of this month, two major wind and tide disasters occurred. In Pudong and other areas, countless people, livestock, fields, and houses were submerged and washed away. Hengsha, Gaodunsha, Yuanyuan, and other three sandbars in Chuansha are isolated in the sea, and the situation is particularly severe. It is now found that apart from the disaster victims who have relatives and friends to turn to and those who have died, there are countless people without food, clothing, or shelter. There are more than 25,000 people in Chuansha, Nanhui, and other areas. The area is barren and the people are poor, and there is no way to provide relief. Therefore, the county magistrates and gentry and merchants of the two counties came to Shanghai for help. We have established this association to ask all sectors to generously donate to accomplish this charitable cause." Next, Wang Xiaolai, Shi Liangcai, and Li Leng, the magistrate of Chuansha County, gave reports in succession (details omitted).

(Dike Collapse) Subsequently, Yuan Xiluo, the magistrate of Nanhui County, reported on the disaster situation, saying, "In the first district of Nanhui County, 3,300 zhang of dikes collapsed. 1,094 zhang of dikes were breached, 592 zhang collapsed, and the remaining 1,600 zhang were also damaged. The second district had 4,300 zhang of dikes, with 1,310 zhang breached and 2,990 zhang collapsed. The rest were also badly damaged. The fourth district had 3,200 zhang of dikes, with 156 zhang breached and 167 zhang collapsed. The rest were also damaged. In total, 2,560 zhang of dikes were breached and 3,749 zhang collapsed."

(Overview of Disaster) The Pudong Fellow Villagers Association's investigation report stated, "The disaster area in the first district of Nanhui is 80,000 mu, affecting 12 townships with a total of 968 households and 4,519 disaster victims. 356 houses collapsed, 12 people died, and 86 people were injured. 37,590 jin of accumulated grain have been distributed. The disaster area in the second district is 50,000 mu, affecting 16 townships with 797 households and 3,809 disaster victims. 471 houses collapsed, 14 people died, and 67 people were injured. 31,900 jin of accumulated grain have been distributed. The disaster area in the fourth district is 20,000 mu, affecting 13 townships with 831 households and 3,851 disaster victims. 211 houses collapsed, 14 people died, and 54 people were injured. 31,220 jin of accumulated grain have been distributed. In total, the disaster area is 150,000 mu, affecting 41 townships with 2,597 households and 12,179 disaster victims. 1,038 houses collapsed, 40 people died, and 207 people were injured. 100,000 jin of accumulated grain have been distributed."

(Resolutions Passed) (1) Send telegrams to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Finance, the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Department of Civil Affairs, and the Department of Finance to allocate funds for relief. (2) Recommend Du Yuesheng, Zhang Gongquan, Wang Xiaolai, Mu Ouchu, Shi Liangcai, Huang Hanzhi, and six others to meet with Finance Minister Song to request relief. (3) Appoint Wang Liangzhong, Jiang Zhuoling, Lu Tongmei, Zhang Yixin, and other four representatives from Nanhui and Chuansha to prepare documents and petition the Jiangsu Provincial Government. (4) Send an inspection team consisting of Mu Ouchu, Zou Bingwen, Xu Jizi, and others to the disaster area for investigation and inspection.

(List of Elected) Then, the election began immediately. As a result, Du Yuesheng was elected as the Chairman of the Committee, Wang Xiaolai and Wang Yiting were elected as the Vice-Chairmen, and Xu Shiying was elected as the Honorary President. The Standing Committee members included Gu Jisheng, Lu Bohong, Yu Qiaqing, Wen Lanting, Guan Jiongzhi, Shi Liangcai, Lin Kanghou, Zhang Gongquan, Qin Runqing, Zhou Weishi, Qian Xinzhi, Rong Zongjing, Zheng Hongnian, Song Hanzhang, Zhao Jinqing, Wang Shoushan, Zhang Xiaolin, Mu Ouchu, Shen Mengfeng, Lu Wenshao, and other nineteen people. The Supervisory Committee members included Wang Yansong, Yu Zuoting, Zhu Yinjiang, Pan Xulun, Gu Xinyi, Hu Junzhuang, Zhang Weiru, Feng Bingnan, Gui Yanfang, Xu Yushu, Huang Jinrong, Shen Zijian, Lu Yuequan, Qu Shao Yi, Yang Qingyuan, Zhang Xiaoliang, Qin Yanqi, Chen Luanqing, Xu Ji Zuo, and other nineteen people. The Executive Committee members included Li Shoushan, Jin Tingsun, Zhang Xianqing, Cheng Yiqing, Weng Yinchu, Chen Zheqing, Bei Songsun, Chen Songyuan, Lao Jingxiu, Lu Qinghua, Yang Zhixiong, Xu Jiling, Wu Yunzhai, Fei Yunqing, Xu Qianlin, Li Dizhou, Zhang Lanping, Jiang Ganting, Huang Xingjie, Huang Yunsheng, Gu Zhuxuan, Xi Yunsheng, Qi Zhongsan, Xu Xinliu, Chen Guangfu, Wang Boyuan, Xu Jingren, Fang Yexian, Yan Fuqing, Dou Yaoting, Feng Youwei, Hu Junqiu, Wang Binyan, Guo Le, Wang Boqi, and other one hundred and twenty-seven people. Huang Renzhi, Pan Zhiwen, Qu Shao Yi, Jiang Zhuoyun, Zhang Bochou, and other five people were appointed as General Affairs, Huang Jinrong, Zhang Xiaolin, Jin Tingsun, and other three people were appointed as Fundraising, Gui Yanfang, Zhang Xiaoliang, Chen Zixin, Yang Yusheng, and other four people were appointed as Finance, Zhang Bohong, Cheng Yiqing, and other two people were appointed as Investigation and Release, Pang Jingzhou, Qu Shaoheng, and other two people were appointed as Hygiene, Shen Zijian was appointed as Statistics, Pan Xulun, Xu Yushu, Chen Luanqing, were appointed as Audit, Mu Ouchu, Zou Bingwen, Xu Ji Zuo, were appointed as Inspection.

(Telegrams Sent) To the National Government of Nanjing, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Interior, the Zhenjiang Provincial Government, the Department of Civil Affairs, and the Department of Finance, greetings. Pudong is unfortunate. Two major wind and tide disasters occurred in winter and late evening, causing dikes and embankments in Chuansha, Nanhui, and coastal areas to collapse. Countless people, livestock, fields, and houses were submerged, especially the three sands of Hengsha, Gaodun, and Yuanyuan in Chuansha, which were completely submerged. Apart from those who have died, there are currently more than 25,000 people in the two counties who have no clothing, food, or shelter and cannot live from day to day. Now, our association is trying its best to provide urgent relief, but our efforts are too weak to be of much help. These disaster victims are all good people. Please quickly allocate funds to save their lives and restore their vitality. Xu Shiying, Chairman of the Shanghai Pudong Wind and Tide Disaster Relief Association,

Du Yuesheng, and others respectfully kowtow.

(Fundraising Appeal) Crossing the Huangpu River to the east, going beyond the Shanghai city area, Chuansha is to the north, and Nanhui is to the south. Villages and hamlets face each other, and the sounds of chickens and dogs can be heard. Wheat is suitable for spring, and cotton and rice are suitable for autumn. Every year, there is a considerable output to supply the food needs of the entire society. In Chuansha County, there are three relatively large sandbars: Hengsha, Gaodunsha, and Yuanyuan. Over the past forty years, dikes have been built to create fields, the population has grown daily, and productivity has advanced daily. On the night of September 2nd this year, a hurricane struck violently, and the tide rose sharply. The residents of the three sandbars were awakened from their sleep by the roaring flood. They climbed onto their roofs, but the roofs collapsed. They climbed the trees, but the trees broke. Men, women, old, and young cried out in the wilderness. In an instant, some families did not know where to go, some elders over ninety years old were on the verge of death but did not die, some three- or four-year-old children cried and searched for their mothers. One farm woman climbed onto the roof but could not hold on, so she grabbed a piece of wood and held it tightly, drifting with the raging current for a day and a night until she reached the coast of Ningbo, where she was rescued and sent back home. In addition, countless families were destroyed and died. Among the reeds and debris, dead people and livestock were piled up, and the stench was overwhelming, making it impossible to pass by without covering one's nose. It is estimated that over eight thousand people were affected by the disaster. On the mainland coast, the dikes in the first, second, and fourth districts of Nanhui collapsed, submerging over 30,000 mu of fertile land. Over two hundred houses were blown down or washed away, and over two thousand shi of grain were flooded. Over a thousand people climbed onto roofs to escape the water. The situation in the fourth and fifth districts of Chuansha to the north was largely similar. At that time, Magistrate Yuan of Nanhui and Magistrate Li of Chuansha, together with enthusiastic locals, personally visited the disaster areas and urgently collected relief funds and supplies, which were distributed quickly. Just as they were gathering, the second hurricane arrived on September 18th. There was a storm all day, and at night, it brought a large sea tide. The dikes of the three sandbars that had not been destroyed were completely breached, and the coastal mainland, east of the third regiment and Laogang in Nanhui, became a vast expanse of water, completely transformed into a swamp. Sixty li of dikes from north to south were all washed into sawtooth shapes. In Chuansha, the Penggong and Huanggong dikes in the eighth and ninth regiments, which had just been hastily repaired, were breached again, and the flood directly approached the Qin Gong dike, eight or nine li from the sea. A family surnamed Cao, with five members, were all swept into the sea. A person surnamed X, an elderly man of seventy-eight years old, was submerged by the flood. Members of the Pudong Fellow Villagers Association who went to inspect and special commissioners from the Chinese Jishi Society who went to distribute relief all said that such a tragic situation was unprecedented in previous years. A person who is injured once and then injured again is called "severely injured." Ancient benevolent people were saddened and prohibited it. A place that experiences one disaster and then another is called "repeated disasters." Ancient historical records recorded and lamented it. Now, those who are lying dead or barely surviving in the bitter wind and rain among the reeds and broken ports are not those whom we call "compatriots"? Are they not the purest and most law-abiding good people of the Republic of China, who repay the country with their blood and sweat? The clothes we wear and the food we eat, if we trace their origins, all come from the hard work of these people throughout the year. Now, those who usually clothe and feed us to live are dead. Those who survived one disaster die in the second. Even if they have not died, they are not far from death. And we who wear their clothes and eat their food, are we to turn a blind eye to their misery as if we do not see it? Are we to turn a deaf ear to the sounds of sorrow that fill our ears as if we do not hear them? Our government and caring people in our society are vigorously advocating "revitalizing the countryside" and "relieving farmers." If we abandon these farmers in the most productive countryside, who have suffered the most severe disasters once and twice, and who are in the most urgent need of relief, and do not plan for relief, it is a loss of conscience in terms of virtue and a misjudgment in terms of politics. Officials of the two counties and local public organizations have gathered all their strength to investigate and provide relief. Nanhui has a larger area and more victims, while Chuansha has a smaller area but has suffered even more severely. The population seeking food is estimated at 10,000 in Chuansha and 15,000 in Nanhui. If each person eats two yuan per month, and only counting four months, 200,000 yuan is needed. There are 3,000 households in Chuansha and 4,000 households in Nanhui without homes. If each household is assisted with 10 yuan for building a house, 70,000 yuan is needed. Each set of winter clothing costs one yuan, requiring 25,000 yuan. This is the current emergency need, totaling no less than 300,000 yuan. The cost of repairing dikes and embankments and the funds for plowing and stabilizing the land next spring are not included in this. The members of this association, remembering that Shanghai is the hub of land and sea transportation, and that the people of Shanghai have always done their best when there are disasters in various places, and have participated in every effort. Now, within a few tens of li of our Shanghai, within one or two weeks, we have encountered major disasters, once and twice, with the loss of hundreds of lives and tens of thousands of people without clothing, food, or homes. "If people want to do good, who is not like me?" We dare not ask for repayment, but we cannot but call on you. We only hope that benevolent people, righteous people, public and private legal entities of the present time will generously assist us with a constant stream. What can be predicted is that the relief funds will not be wasted, and the relief efforts will all be practical. All income and expenditure will be publicly reported. We only seek to save one more disaster victim, to preserve one more good farmer's life, and thus to maintain one more source of production. The vast flood, the floating white bones, living as hardworking farmers in summer fields, dying as floating corpses in autumn tides, we dare to wipe away our tears and beg for your generous donations.

Page 11

The Municipal Government's Opinion on the Factory Inspection Case

The Bureau of Public Works Has No Right to Formulate Labor Regulations

Still Hoping to Maintain the Spirit of Cooperation as Always

Do Not Persist in Unreasonable Claims

Central News Agency reports that regarding the negotiation on the factory inspection case in the Concession, because the Municipal Government representative refused the Bureau of Public Works' proposal that the inspection team formed by both parties should be supervised by the Bureau, similar to the method of collecting stamp tax and special cigarette tax, the situation has reached a stalemate. As reported in the previous news, the reporter, after seeing the propaganda published by the North-China Daily News yesterday, in order to understand our side's attitude, specially visited a municipal official, who made the following remarks:

The Chinese government, in view of the fact that factories in Shanghai have repeatedly caused disasters due to poor equipment or management, resulting in numerous deaths and injuries, and in order to protect the safety of workers, improve the conditions of workers, and promote harmonious labor-capital relations, believes that factory inspection is a matter of urgency. Since factories in the Concession account for two-thirds of the city's factories, if it is not implemented simultaneously, the handling will inevitably encounter many obstacles, so officials were sent to consult with the Concession authorities. For half a year, the representatives of both parties repeatedly studied and drafted a compromise plan. It was heard that after the plan was submitted to the board meeting of the Bureau, the other party suddenly proposed that the inspection team should be supervised by them, which greatly affected the progress of the case, which is deeply regrettable. The Bureau of Public Works, knowing that it is not allowed to formulate labor regulations in the Concession to be followed by taxpayers, initially wanted to obtain a legal basis for managing factories by revising Article 34 of the Yangjingbang Regulations Annex. Then, it considered citing the provisions of Article 35 of the Annex, which deal with the prohibition of dangerous businesses, to expand its powers and achieve the purpose of managing factories. Regarding the former, the Bureau of Public Works cannot seize our country's administrative power by revising the annex, because the territorial rights in the Concession still belong to our country, and the Chinese people in the Concession do not sever their natural and legal relationship with our government simply because they reside in the Concession. Regarding the latter, the so-called dangerous businesses should have a clear interpretation and a reasonable scope. If they are forcibly attached and arbitrarily prohibited, Chinese merchants in the Concession will be unable to operate happily. Foreigners often think that the Chinese authorities are being troublesome by insisting on sovereignty, but anyone who understands the history of the Shanghai Concession knows that the Bureau of Public Works cannot be compared to ordinary municipal agencies. Its legal status and powers are clearly limited, and its encroachments on its authority should not be ignored. Factory inspection cannot be delayed any longer. The Chinese government sincerely hopes that the Concession authorities will consider the seriousness of this issue, maintain the spirit of cooperation as always, and not persist in claims that are unreasonable in law and reason, so that this case can be resolved as soon as possible.

The Sino-Foreign Relief Association Recently Received a Report from a Disaster Investigation Specialist

The Sino-Foreign Relief Association received reports and telegrams about the flood disasters in the North and South, indicating the extreme seriousness of the situation. For Chongming and other areas, it specially dispatched specialist Chai Yeyu to investigate. Zheng Shouchun had already been dispatched to Luyu and other provinces to conduct an on-the-ground survey. The reports received from Chai and Zheng on the same day yesterday are recorded as follows:

Chongming Chai Yeyu's report: "I arrived in Chongming yesterday and first rushed to the most severely affected Fifth District. This district is located in the west of Chongming, bordering the sea and the river. In past years, it has always been the first to bear the brunt of disasters. This time, it was just hit by the Jiangye catastrophe, and by chance, it was hit by a second hurricane the next night, the scope of which was even larger than before. All the dikes were destroyed for 30 miles, and countless fields were submerged. More than 2,000 households inside the head dike were completely washed away. In addition to the disaster victims who can be taken in by relatives or scattered in all directions, there are still more than 10,000 people in urgent need of relief. Yeyu then went with the food relief boat of the district office. Everywhere he passed, it was a vast expanse of water. It was very difficult for the disaster victims to go to the town to seek food because they were surrounded by deep water and had no strength to swim, and many starved to death. When they heard that the food relief boat had arrived, they cried out in sorrow, which could be heard for several miles. The situation was extremely tragic. Many old and weak people, because they were in pain because they had no clothes, no food, and no home to return to, were willing to sit and wait for death and did not want to survive. Because they had not eaten for many days, they lay in the holes in the embankment, with faint voices and no strength to move. According to the villagers, this time the fields were filled with salt water, and it will be difficult to plant in the spring next year. The dikes must be repaired urgently, or there may be hope. If this continues, the fields will forever turn into lakes and ponds. According to reports, after the two hurricanes in Chongming, except for the Sixth District, which was relatively less affected, all the other districts were severely affected, especially the Fifth and Third Districts."

Chengwu Zheng Shouchun's report: "I have arrived in Chengwu County, Shandong, and traveled throughout the area. The water in the east and west districts has not receded to this day. The old Yellow River area is still one or two feet deep. Only half of the land can be used to grow grain. Most of the salt-producing areas have been submerged. A total of 360 villages have been flooded, and more than 4,100 hectares of farmland have been submerged. There are more than 60,000 disaster victims, and the losses are estimated at more than 1.8 million yuan." The association believes that the waters from the breaches of the Yellow River have not yet receded, and Chongming and other counties have been hit by two hurricanes. The weather has turned cold in autumn, and the disaster victims in various places are starving and freezing, waiting for relief. However, it is difficult to raise relief funds, and it is difficult to provide universal relief. The association is deeply worried and hopes that all sectors will quickly lend a helping hand to save the survivors of this water disaster.

Beijing-Shanghai Railway Announces the Content of Central Loan "Surplus Profit Certificates"

A total of 580,000 pounds were issued, limited to 50 years for repayment.

The total amount of surplus profits paid is more than 2.8 million yuan.

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway was built with a loan from the Chinese and British Bank. Among them, there is a type of "surplus profit certificate," with a total amount of 500,000 gold pounds. The total amount of surplus profits over the years has reached more than 3.37 million yuan. The content of the certificate is mostly unknown to the outside world. Now the Railway Bureau specially announces its content and process as follows:

(Issuance Process) According to Article 12 of the railway loan contract, one-fifth of the surplus profits of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway should belong to the Chinese and British Bank. Therefore, "surplus profit certificates" were issued at one-fifth of the total cost value of the railway, with a face value of 200 English pounds per certificate, and issued in installments at the same time as the loan notes. The amount of each time depends on the amount of loan notes issued, up to one-fifth of the total amount. The annual income of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, in addition to the payment of various expenses, road maintenance, station repairs, addition and replacement of locomotives, and office expenses, as well as the annual interest rate of 5% for the loan notes and the annual interest rate of 6% for the land price purchased by the China Railway Corporation itself or borrowed from other silver companies, is all surplus profit. One-fifth of the surplus profit is submitted to the silver company for distribution to the holders of the surplus profit certificates.

(Total Amount and Time Limit) The "surplus profit certificates" are issued at one-fifth of the actual loan amount of 2.9 million pounds for the railway, for a total of 580,000 pounds, with a term of 50 years. However, within the 50-year period, China can redeem them at any time at the original face value. The certificates will be invalidated after the expiration date, without the need for redemption. However, before redemption or before the expiration date, the surplus profits that the railway should distribute according to the regulations must still be distributed before they can be cancelled.

(Surplus Profits Paid) The Sino-British loan contract states that "surplus profit certificates" do not pay interest. The actual amount of the surplus profit issued and not issued over the years since 1921 (previous years had no surplus) is shown in the following table:

1921: 361,346.10 yuan, paid in full in September 1922

1922: 345,669.63 yuan, paid in full in September 1923

1923: 45,661.63 yuan, paid in full in September 1924

1924: 343,861.29 yuan, paid in full in September 1927

1925: 201,373.79 yuan, paid in full in September 1928

1926: 176,336.81 yuan

1927: 105,437.00 yuan, paid in full in September 1929

1928: 392,940.46 yuan

1929: 498,839.20 yuan, paid in installments in August 1930

1930: 241,020.97 yuan, unpaid

1931: 293,249.59 yuan, unpaid

Total: 3,375,736.47 yuan

According to the above table, as of the end of 1931, the total amount of surplus profits was 3,375,736.47 yuan, of which 2,841,465.91 yuan had been paid, and 534,270.56 yuan had not been paid.

Resolution of Disputes Between the Two Exchanges Regarding the Merger of Financial Markets

Du Yuesheng and Zhang Xiaolin mediate

Plan to raise 2 million to organize a new market

According to the Huadong News Agency, regarding the merger of the two gold markets in Shanghai, the Ministry of Industry, considering the difficulties of the merchants, granted an extension of three months after the expiration date of May 31 of this year, as the two parties had not yet reached an agreement. The extension was until August 31, and no further extensions were allowed, to show the government's attitude. However, the authorities of the two exchanges still failed to merge due to their respective rights and interests. The Ministry of Industry then indicated that they would forcibly close the exchanges. Fortunately, Du Yuesheng and Zhang Xiaolin, prominent figures in the business community, took the initiative to mediate, and a formal resolution was reached on the 24th of this month. A reporter from the Huadong News Agency inquired with the authorities of the two exchanges yesterday, and the details are as follows:

(Telegram Requesting Extension) According to the law, the Ministry of Industry originally required the merger of the two exchanges to be resolved before May 31 of this year. However, at that time, the Goods Exchange only merged the securities part with the Huashang Securities Exchange, while the gold part still failed to negotiate a resolution with the Gold Exchange. Therefore, the Ministry of Industry granted a further extension of three months to allow for a more leisurely discussion and indicated that no further extensions would be allowed after the expiration date. However, as of August 31, the attitudes of the two exchanges were still difficult to reconcile. Therefore, the Ministry of Industry indicated that it would forcibly close the exchanges and reorganize them separately. Du Yuesheng and Zhang Xiaolin heard about this and took the initiative to mediate. They also telegraphed the Ministry of Industry to allow continued operations during the mediation period. The Ministry of Industry agreed, and the mediation work began.

(Successful Mediation) The reason why the negotiations between the two exchanges had not been resolved was the issue of the rights of both parties, such as the control of brokers and the selection of the market. Initially, Yu Qiaqing, the chairman of the Goods Exchange, and Xu Pusheng, the chairman of the Gold Exchange, had several discussions, but they could not reach an agreement. At one point, it was proposed to set up two separate gold markets, Gold Market No. 1 and No. 2, so that the names would be unified and the operations could be the same, but this also failed to reach an agreement. After Du and Zhang took the initiative to mediate, they summoned Yu and Xu to have an open and honest discussion, proceeding on the principle of equality and mutual benefit, and put forward a plan. Both parties were satisfied and signed a contract on the spot on the 24th of this month at the Hangzhou Restaurant, formally resolving the dispute.

(Separate Organization) After this mediation was established, both parties decided to abolish the original names of the two exchanges and jointly form a new exchange as the only financial market in Shanghai. The capital was set at 2 million yuan. The name, address, and how to organize the exchange will be determined by first organizing a preparatory committee, with Yu Qiaqing and Xu Pusheng as members of the preparatory committee. Du and Zhang will also join to ensure that the progress of both parties does not give rise to any further disagreements.

(Establishment in Two Months) According to the authorities of the two exchanges, the name and location of the exchange have not yet been determined. Whether the address will be selected from one of the two exchanges or purchased separately will depend on whether the transportation is convenient. During the preparation period for the new market, the two exchanges will continue to operate as usual. The authorities of the two exchanges and the mediators Du and Zhang have telegraphed the Ministry of Industry separately for verification. As for when the new market will be established, Sheng Buhua of the Goods Exchange told reporters that it would probably be within one or two months and would not be protracted.

(Citywide Unity) The reason why the Ministry of Industry ordered the merger was that the Exchange Law stipulates that there should not be two markets of the same nature in the same area, to avoid confusion in the market situation. Now that the merger of the two exchanges has been resolved, there will be no further disputes in Shanghai after the new market is organized. The gold market can also be unified. Also, when the dispute between the two exchanges was unresolved, merchants in Shanghai, such as Zhang Danru, submitted a request to the Social Affairs Bureau, which was forwarded to the Municipal Government, proposing to set up a Gold and Silver Exchange so that the financial market would not be interrupted if the negotiations between the two exchanges broke down and the Ministry of Industry forcibly closed the exchanges. Now that the merger issue has been resolved, there is no need to set up a separate Gold and Silver Exchange that is in preparation.

Wharf Strike Disrupts Silk and Tea Export Delays

Numerous European and American Goods Obstructed in Huangpu River

Merchants Negotiating with Wheelock Marden for Losses

Wheelock Marden's barge transportation services play a crucial role in Shanghai's foreign export trade. The company owns over 150 barges of various sizes and employs more than 400 barge workers. The recent strike caused by worker layoffs has lasted for nearly twenty days. Although a settlement was initially reached a few days ago, with workers agreeing to return to work, negotiations subsequently broke down again, and the strikers have not resumed work. This has had a significant impact on Shanghai's exports. Merchants, concerned about the obstruction of goods, have been questioning Wheelock Marden and demanding compensation for their losses. The recent situation is detailed below:

(Large Quantities of Chinese Tea Blocked) When ships depart from Shanghai, merchants entrust the valuable goods to Wheelock Marden's barges for transportation, as they are considered more reliable. On the 19th of this month, the British mail steamer "Ellora" was scheduled to sail to England, carrying 700 chests of high-quality Chinese tea from Shanghai to London. The merchants entrusted the tea to Wheelock Marden's barges for transfer. However, a strike suddenly broke out while the tea was loaded onto the barges, resulting in all the tea being blocked on the barges and unable to be transferred to the mail steamer. Despite repeated negotiations between the merchants and Wheelock Marden, no solution has been found. The goods remain on the barges in the Huangpu River as of yesterday.

(Shipment of Goods to America Also Delayed) Furthermore, over 200 tons of goods destined for New York, USA, have also been blocked by the strike after being loaded onto Wheelock Marden's barges. The shipping company's attempt to send workers to unload the goods was rejected by the strikers. In addition, a large quantity of pig bristles and silk waste, destined for Marseille, France, has also been held up and cannot be loaded onto the ship. The merchants have had to postpone the shipment, rescheduling the loading of these blocked goods for October 3rd. However, it remains uncertain whether the situation will be resolved by then.

(Merchants Negotiating for Losses) The merchants argue that the delays caused by the Wheelock Marden barge strike for items such as silk and tea affect the market prices when the goods arrive in Europe and America. Furthermore, the export of goods is based on estimated arrival dates, which are related to bank financing and marine insurance. The recipients of the goods also suffer significantly due to market demand. Therefore, valuable goods must be loaded onto regular mail steamers, which have fixed arrival times. The current delay of over fourteen days caused by the barge strike has had a ripple effect on all aspects of the trade. The merchants have suffered substantial losses and are now sending letters to Wheelock Marden, demanding that the company bear the full cost of the delayed exports.

Fellow Tradesmen Become Bitter Enemies Seeking to Kill Each Other

Purchasing Guns to Avenge Grievances

Fortunately, Detectives Apprehend the Suspect

Wang Heqing, a small carpentry foreman from Ningbo, 33 years old, residing in a shack at 8 Feihong Road, Zhabei, recently developed an irreconcilable feud with Mao Laosan, a small painting foreman. The conflict arose when Wang contracted for a construction job, which Mao allegedly seized by force. Wang confronted Mao, who brandished a pistol and threatened to kill Wang. Filled with anger, Wang secretly commissioned someone to buy a five-shot pistol from a foreign ship, intending to retaliate and assassinate Mao Laosan. Mao learned of this and secretly reported it to the Hongkou Police Station. Western Detective C. S. Goodworth and Chinese Detective Zhang Bingchen intercepted Wang Heqing. During questioning, Wang confessed to hiding the pistol at home. He was escorted to the Fifth District, Third Precinct, requesting police assistance in searching his house. Precinct Chief Wen dispatched police officer Zhan Chuan, who accompanied them to Wang's house and found a five-shot pistol and five bullets. The items were taken to the police station for verification. Precinct Chief Wen, considering Wang Heqing's audacity in possessing a gun for revenge, a violation of criminal law, handed the defendant over to the detectives for further investigation. However, the pistol and bullets, having been seized in the interior, were kept in accordance with regulations. Yesterday, a formal report was submitted to the General Bureau for review. Furthermore, it was discovered that Mao Laosan, residing on Xinmin Road in Zhabei, within the jurisdiction of the Fourth District, was also not a good person, engaging in aggressive behavior with weapons in a business dispute. It is requested that all district police stations and detective teams be instructed to jointly apprehend him and severely punish him as a warning to others.

Two Unusual Birds Suddenly Appear at the National Products Exhibition

Feathers of Mottled Colors Resembling Phoenixes

They Immediately Flapped Their Wings and Flew South

Around 7:00 AM on the previous morning, amidst a light drizzle, two large birds suddenly flew into the National Products Exhibition Hall in the Penglai Market, Xiaoximen. They perched on the square pavilion of the Yabu Er Electric Factory's booth, standing motionless and appearing very tame. The birds' feathers were mottled with five colors, and their necks were particularly long, resembling the phoenixes seen in paintings. Their size was comparable to that of peacocks. When a staff member from the Dalong Woolen Mill discovered them, a commotion arose as all the exhibition staff rushed to observe. The two birds soon flapped their wings and flew north, perching on the roof of the northern commercial area of the exhibition hall. After about half an hour, they flew swiftly south and disappeared, leaving the onlookers marveling at the sight.

New Developments in the European Steel Industry

Belgian Sales Office Establishes Branch in Shanghai

Since the European steel industry has been affected by intense competition and economic downturn, it has made every effort to reorganize. In May of this year, steel manufacturers in Belgium, France, Germany, Luxembourg, and other countries formed an agreement to limit the total annual steel production of the four countries to 6.8 million tons. The distribution is as follows: Belgium 29%, Germany 29%, France 21%, and Luxembourg 21%. Historically, the sale of Belgian steel has largely relied on export companies in London, Hamburg, Antwerp, and Saarlouis, resulting in price discrepancies and making unified management difficult. Various plans have been proposed to remedy this, but none have fully satisfied all parties. Belgian manufacturers lack a centralized sales organization, so most have established their own export companies to sell their products. Among these, the United Sales Office of Belgian Steel Factories is the most well-known. Its export volume accounts for nearly 60% of Belgium's total production, and its affiliated factories are all the most complete and modern steel mills in Belgium. Belgian steel products sold in China amount to over 100,000 tons annually, accounting for over 32% of imports, making it an important market. It is reported that the office has established a branch in Shanghai to facilitate direct transactions with Chinese merchants and enable them to obtain goods at prices set by the original factories. The branch is managed by the Banque Belge Pour L'Etranger at 6 Jiujiang Road.

Yuan Yugen, Young and Ambitious

Commits Suicide by Hanging Due to Minor Losses

Yitai Shun South Goods and Seafood Store, located at 72 Zhaojia Road, Dadongmen, Nanshi, was reopened in mid-March of this year by Ningbo native Yuan Yugen (23 years old, from Zhenhai) and his fellow townsman Wang Shanqing, with a total share capital of 6,000 yuan. Wang served as the manager, and Yuan as the assistant manager. However, since taking over the business, the store's operations have remained sluggish. With the Mid-Autumn Festival approaching, a recent accounting revealed minor losses. Yuan became deeply troubled, feeling ashamed towards the shareholders, and expressing a pessimistic attitude. Unexpectedly, around 4:00 PM the day before, the store's employee Shi Liqing, along with the cook Wu Haijiang and apprentice Xu Jiankun, went upstairs and noticed that Yuan's door was tightly closed and there was no sound inside. They knocked on the door but received no response. Sensing something amiss, they quickly informed the accountant, who forced the door open. They found Yuan had hanged himself. They immediately took him down and felt that his body was still slightly warm. They rushed him to the nearby Qu Zhibu Hospital for treatment, but it was too late. He had already died. They immediately reported the incident to the Second Precinct of the First District. Chief Liu immediately sent a patrol officer to investigate. It was also reported that the deceased had sent a letter to his hometown of Ningbo the day before his death, presumably a suicide note. It is said that Yuan had been engaged to be married in his hometown in March of this year.

If it is in the country, with private commercial shipping being much more numerous than state-owned shipping, it does not seem appropriate to cite it as an example.

Mechanical Engineering Association Cables Request that Examinations Emphasize Experience

The Shanghai Mechanical Engineering Association submitted a report to the Minister of Communications, stating: "Regarding the newly promulgated Provisional Regulations for the Examination and Determination of Seafarers, the examination subjects emphasize academics, which should be amended to benefit the shipping industry and encourage mechanical engineering talent. The Department of Navigation under the Ministry issued a letter on September 8, promulgating regulations and implementation rules such as the Provisional Regulations for the Examination and Determination of Seafarers, stipulating that all deck officers or marine engineers on domestic ships must be certified as qualified by the Ministry and issued certificates before they can serve. We see that the Ministry attaches importance to the shipping industry and identifying marine engineering talent, which coincides with the Association's aim to strictly prevent unqualified seafarers. Although the provisions are quite comprehensive, there are still some areas that are somewhat lacking in terms of foresight. We humbly submit this to the Ministry. Since the signing of the Treaty of Nanjing by the Qing Court, foreigners have controlled the customs and shipping rights have been lost. All important seafarers, such as chief engineers, have been foreigners. The government at the time was accustomed to it for a long time and there was no way to remedy it. Those who have a glimmer of light rely on our Chinese seafarers to work hard in the shipping industry and seek to become skilled and experienced, so that foreigners believe that the service ability and efficiency of Chinese officers are not inferior to those of foreign officers. It was not until 1914, when the European War broke out and marine engineers from various countries returned home to serve, that foreigners felt the need and recognized that the Chinese who were practicing marine engineering had the ability to serve as chief engineers. The Marine Department of the Customs then allowed Chinese officers with rich marine engineering experience who passed the oral examination to serve as chief engineers, etc. There are now many Chinese officers serving in this position. But tracing back to the past, all of our Chinese officers relied on rich experience and skilled skills to fight for this right through long-term struggles in difficult and arduous conditions. It was not merely that possessing a diploma and book qualification could bring good fortune. The Ministry's examination of seafarers emphasizes examinations, which is truly in line with the need to select specialized talents. The Association also hopes that the implementation of the examination can create a long-term strategy for traffic safety and eliminate the unqualified. However, there is still a need to consider the examination methods. According to Article 16, Item B of the Implementation Rules of the Provisional Regulations for the Examination and Determination of Seafarers, the written examination subjects for marine engineers include Chinese, English or other foreign languages, general knowledge of mechanics, including mathematics, mechanics, physics, etc., and marine engineering and drawing. A score of 50% or more in each written examination subject is required to pass. According to the marine engineers' operating business, they use marine engines day and night to break through thousands of miles, and they are more than capable of using marine engines. In terms of their rich experience, they certainly have the strengths in the application of the above-mentioned subjects. However, if they are required to present the mathematical formulas or principle diagrams of what they have experienced in order to meet the qualifications for the examination, it is truly not a good way to cultivate marine engineering talent. This is the first reason why the examination should emphasize the results of work experience and not emphasize academics. After 1914, the Customs examination and selection of chief engineers emphasized oral examinations, focusing on the marine engineers' daily marine engineering practice experience and their actual work, without emphasizing books and theories as the criteria for admission. Those who were admitted were all able to perform their duties well, because their experience was rich and their work was detailed. Although they did not thoroughly study books and theories, it was not difficult for them to use their experience to deal with their business. This is the second reason that should be considered. Furthermore, according to Articles 3, Items 5-8 and Article 4 of the above-mentioned regulations, the service years from two to eight years are used as the standard for original-level examination and promotion examination, respectively. It is clear that work experience is not inferior to academic subjects, but the examination focuses solely on academic subjects as the criteria for admission, which is inconsistent with the original purpose. The Association believes that the examination of marine engineers cannot be delayed, but the scores for the oral examination subjects should be set at 50% for marine engineering management application cabin operation experience work performance, etc., 20% for general subjects, and 30% for marine engineering subjects. This matter is related to the good strategy of the shipping industry and the maintenance of marine engineering talent. It is necessary to consider all aspects and not make marine engineers who have been struggling in China's shipping industry feel regret because the examination regulations are not comprehensive enough and place too much emphasis on academic subjects. It is reasonable to submit this to the Ministry of Communications and request that the Provisional Regulations for the Examination and Determination of Seafarers be amended as appropriate and then re-examined, which will be beneficial. This report is submitted to Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Communications."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Cables Request to Lift the Ban on Setting Off Firecrackers

Safeguarding the Livelihood of the Firecracker Industry Workers

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce telegraphed the Nanjing Executive Yuan and the Zhenjiang Provincial Government yesterday, stating: (Omitted titles) On the 11th and 14th of this month, according to a letter from the Firecracker Industry Association, it was reported that on August 29th, it was reported that the Songjiang County Government, upon order of the Provincial Government, determined that the sound of firecrackers and guns was easily confused, and that in the event of a bandit alarm in the future, it was especially feared, so it decided to take measures to ban them, and immediately ordered the town and village chiefs to order the town and village police to use gongs to announce that from September 3rd, it would be strictly prohibited. The sound of firecrackers rings twice in succession, unlike the sound of guns, which rings once or up to five or six times, and the sound it emits, although difficult to describe in words, is clearly and obviously different. Even ignorant men and women know this. Moreover, in recent years, thieves have risen everywhere in our country. The reason for this is that there are too many people and too little gruel, resulting in many unemployed people in society who cannot make a living. As a result, they disregard their lives, take risks, and become thieves. As the saying goes, people are driven by hunger and cold, and have no sense of shame. This is not false. Speaking of those who work in the firecracker industry, there are statistics everywhere, and there are tens of thousands in each place. The number of their families who depend on them for support is even unknown. If a strict ban is imposed, those who directly and indirectly depend on them for a living will inevitably have nowhere to turn and become thieves, and social order will inevitably become more chaotic. If this is the case, it will not only fail to appease the people, but will harm them. It is truly feared that it will backfire. The Chamber of Commerce, in view of this, for the sake of the livelihood of the industry and the country and society, dares to offend your esteemed council and requests that you forward a letter to the Jiangsu Provincial Government to take into account both the livelihood of the firecracker industry people and local security, and to deliberate on a flexible approach, and to instruct all subordinate county governments to strictly comply. We will be deeply grateful. It has always been the case that the order to ban the setting off of firecrackers is only issued when martial law is enforced in the locality. There is currently no military activity in the province of Su, and the locality is peaceful, which is not comparable to the time of martial law. Guns have been popular in China and have been used by the army for a long time, but firecrackers have an even older origin, and have been commonly used in civilian celebrations and mourning ceremonies for a long time. In times of order and tranquility, there have never been any misunderstandings or panics. If they are banned regardless of whether martial law is in effect, it is tantamount to exterminating the firecracker industry, which will cause hundreds of thousands of shopkeepers who sell firecrackers and workers who make firecrackers in various provinces to lose their jobs, which will not help to maintain order and tranquility, but will only increase unemployment and panic, leading to hidden dangers in the locality. From ancient times, governing is about nurturing the people first, and enabling them to support themselves second. Today, the country's financial resources are not able to carry out large-scale operations to enable the unemployed to cultivate the land, but the policies issued are to deprive the people of their self-sufficiency. It is believed that this is not permissible. Recently, the Dutch East Indies, Batavia, also issued an order prohibiting overseas Chinese from setting off firecrackers. The overseas Chinese protested against this, saying that the government should not interfere in religious rituals. Now, a similar ban is being issued in the country, which makes it even more difficult for overseas Chinese to negotiate with foreign countries. The firecracker industry is under internal and external pressure, and can only tend towards extinction. Therefore, we dare not avoid offending you and sincerely request that your esteemed council review and approve the lifting of the aforementioned ban in order to maintain the livelihood of the firecracker industry. This will be in the public interest. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce kowtows.

Reconciliation in the Case of Feng Qiwen Being Sued by Xiao Lin Daiyu

Feng Qiwen, a Ningbo native residing at No. 12, Dapu Lane, Jin Shenfu Road, French Concession, formerly employed at the Guangdong Bank, now forty-one years old, previously, due to having no sons, married the prostitute Zhu Mao Yuan (age twenty this year, also known as Xiao Lin Daiyu A Yuan), a Zhenjiang native, as a concubine at the end of the twentieth year, and rented a house to live together. In the fourth month of the old calendar this year, she gave birth to a girl, and suddenly a difference of opinion arose, and he abandoned the girl and the child. Mao Yuan and her mother, Zhu Li, hired lawyers such as Tu Zhenhu to act as agents, and filed a criminal self-accusation with the First Special District Court, accusing Feng of seduction and abandonment, and also filed a civil lawsuit, requesting a judgment to pay for living expenses. Feng also hired a lawyer to defend himself. The details of the interrogation have been reported in previous newspapers. The case was repeatedly summoned to court, and the parties were ordered to reconcile out of court, but the two sides could not resolve the matter due to the large difference in the amount of the civil lawsuit. It is now heard that the case has been vigorously mediated by lawyers, relatives, and friends of both parties, and Feng Qiwen has given Mao Yuan four hundred yuan, and the child born is unconditionally handed over to Feng to take back for upbringing. A reconciliation has been reached, and the plaintiff has filed a request with the court to withdraw the lawsuit.

Car Overturns

Three People Injured

Shen Chuande, a doctor at the Tiren Hospital on Julu Road, French Concession, age twenty-eight, a local, residing at No. 15, Youzhili, Machine Factory Street, Hugunjun Camp, Nanshi, was requested by a patient to visit No. XX, Yuanfang Road, Hongkou yesterday morning at eleven o'clock. Shen had a small Austin car and ordered his driver, Zhu Zhangfu, to drive. When he was returning to Nanshi after the visit, the car was passing the intersection of Broadway and Nanzun Road. Zhu Zhangfu, being a novice driver with poor driving skills, caused one of the car's wheels to get stuck in the tram tracks. For a time, he could not get out. A truck was approaching head-on, creating a dangerous situation. Zhu saw this situation and was at a loss. He then stepped on the accelerator and reversed the car. The car body was too light and overturned, injuring Zhu Zhangfu's hands and face, apprentice Lu Zhixiang's chest, and Shen Chuande's right hand was fractured, causing serious injuries. Later, someone reported this to the police station No. 719, and they were sent to Renji Hospital for treatment.

Robbery on Haining Road Three Years Ago Snatched the Thief

The Victim No Longer Remembers the Thief's Face

The Thief Admits to Having Followed Others to Rob Land

The home of the Lin Zhang family, a Huzhou woman residing at No. 1685, Fushou Lane, Haining Road, was suddenly broken into by four robbers on January 4th, 19th year of the Republic of China, at 9:50 am, on the pretext of asking for letters. The robbers drove four men and ten women in the room into a corner under surveillance, and then went upstairs to search the Lin's and several tenants' homes for gold and silver jewelry, clothes, and silver dollars, valued at 1,163 yuan. They carried the stolen goods and fled. Afterwards, Lin Zhang and others reported this to the Huisi Police Station, requesting an investigation, but it has been three years and the case has not been solved. Until 10:30 am the day before yesterday, Cui Shunk, Ma Derong, and others from the Xinzha Police Station learned that Wang A'gen, a Shaoxing native and a robber in this case, was hiding at No. 23, Xinkaihe, French Concession. They then went with the French Police Station detectives to arrest Wang and brought him back to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the First Special District Court. Yao Tang, a lawyer from the police station, stated the case, saying that several tenants lived at No. 1685, Haining Road, and were all robbed. Today, only Lin Zhang is present, so he requested a postponement for further questioning. Lin Zhang also testified about the robbery, but could not remember the faces of the robbers because three years had passed. When asked, the defendant Wang A'gen confessed that three years ago, when I went to Bao Yu Lane, No. 12, Yanzi Nest, French Concession to smoke opium, I met a friend, Su A'san, who said that Xiao Guangdong had reported that a certain family on Haining Road, Hongkou, was hiding opium, and asked if we wanted to rob it together. We then discussed it there. At that time, Xiao Guangdong and A'qing each held a handgun, and A'san and I went empty-handed. When we arrived, I only stood outside the door. The three of them went inside. After a while, they came out and met at Baoyu Lane to divide the spoils. Later, according to Xiao Guangdong and others, they robbed a total of 20 liang of opium, sold it for 30 yuan, so I was given 5 yuan, etc. After Judge Wu Tingqi verified the confession, he ordered Wang to be detained and to be questioned again in seven days.

Woman Sighed at Wasted Years and Quarrelled with Mother and Committed Suicide by Hanging Herself

The woman Shen Zhang, who lived at No. 121, Laiyi Wharf Road, Dongjiadu, Nanshi, had a daughter named Sanyuan, aged 27, who was not yet married. She often sighed at her advanced age and wasted time, and was always unhappy. The night before, after arguing with her mother over a trivial matter, she became resentful and decided to end her life. She hanged herself alone in the bedroom. At about 3:00 am yesterday morning, she was spotted by a family member, who tried to untie her and rescue her, but to no avail. She died soon after. They then reported it to the First Precinct, First Station of the Public Security Bureau, who sent personnel to investigate and instructed the land guard to report to the court for an autopsy.

Hongkou Police Arrest Bandits

Chinese and Western detectives from the Hongkou Police Station arrested eight bandits, Shaoxing native Li Fengchun, Yangzhou native Xu Xueshu, Wang Jinsheng, Zhang A'mao, etc., in Tangshan Road, Fujian Road, and Julu Road in the French Concession yesterday morning around 8:00 am. They confiscated two handguns and eight bullets and brought them to the police station. After investigating, it was found that these people had committed several robberies in the concession, so they informed the police chief and ordered them to be detained and sent to the court for interrogation.

Fire on Connaught Road

At 10:35 am yesterday morning, a fire broke out at the home of Xu Jingming, a Suzhou native residing at No. 16, Longxing Lane, Connaught Road, Huxi. It was caused by carelessness while cooking, which resulted in a fire that quickly spread to the firewood, causing dense smoke. Fortunately, neighbors fought to put out the fire immediately, limiting the damage to bedding and other items. It was only when the dense smoke was billowing up that two relatives from Dongting Mountain, Xu Laowu and Wu Yunsheng, who had just arrived in Shanghai a few days ago and were living upstairs, panicked and jumped out of the window, causing them to fall to the ground. Xu injured his head and legs, and Wu injured his waist, back, and legs. They were bleeding profusely and were in a coma. The Caojiadu Fire Brigade drove to the scene and immediately lifted the two injured men into the vehicle and sent them to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. The Sixth District then sent police officers to detain the fire starter, Xu Jingming, for punishment.

Ni Shanchang of Zhenye Thermos Factory Goes to the Southwest to Investigate Market Conditions

The Huoche Brand thermos bottles produced by the Zhenye Thermos Bottle Factory on Wenjian Shi Road, Hongkou, have been welcomed by patriotic people since they were launched. Letter

To whom it may concern, I recently read a news item in your newspaper on the 25th of this month that the police at the South Station were inspecting items and detaining those without invoices, causing merchants to complain. This is not in accordance with the facts. It was found that on the 22nd of this month, when police officer Dai Shangxian was inspecting goods at the South Railway Station, he saw Wang Malin carrying cloth and looking flustered. When asked if he had an invoice for the cloth and where he bought it, he was dumbfounded and could not answer. He also offered four jiao of small foreign money to bribe the officer to let him go. Afterwards, our district chief ordered him to present solid evidence or a reliable guarantor. Wang Malin then claimed that the cloth was bought from a teahouse and that the seller could not be found, and that he did not know any stores in Shanghai. Because the circumstances were suspicious, the witness was sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. On the 24th, Shou Kanghua shipped many rubber overshoes without invoices. When the police officers inquired, Shou attempted to escape, so he was taken to the district. Afterwards, the Ximeihua Clothing Store provided proof, and he was released. There was no "detention of goods carried by passengers without invoices."

The facts are as stated above. Please investigate, correct, and disclose the truth. To the Shenbao. Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, Second District Office. September 26.

Educational News

Reduced Fare for Athletic Meet Officials and Athletes

One-Quarter Fare Reduction

Telegraphic Dispatch No. 2057 from the Ministry of Railways to the Two Route Administrations: Approving the Ministry of Education's communication regarding the request from the Preparatory Committee of the 22nd National Athletic Meet to follow the precedent of the 20th Meet, allowing officials, athletes, and referees to receive fare reductions for train travel. As this meet is to fulfill the unfinished mission of the 20th National Athletic Meet, it is agreed to assist by following the previous example. The committee will issue fare reduction certificates to officials and athletes, allowing them to purchase tickets at one-quarter of the regular fare. Referees traveling to Beijing from various locations will be issued free travel certificates. Full-price tickets must be purchased for sleeper berths for both types of certificates. Each free travel certificate for referees is limited to one person; multiple people cannot use a single certificate. Ticket inspectors on trains should strictly verify the referees' names against the list and rigorously enforce the precautions listed on the certificates to prevent abuses. Sample fare reduction certificates, sample free travel certificates, a list of referee departure stations, a rough table of the number of athletes from various routes, and a list of meet officials, fifteen copies each, are being sent for prompt compliance.

Jinan Continues to Win the Jiangda Swimming Championship for Three Years

Jiaotong Second, Fudan Third, Daxia Fourth, Guanghua Fifth

Jiaotong Lacks Long-Distance Talent, Women's Competition Temporarily Changed to Performance

Jiaotong Yu Rongbang Breaks Jiangda 50-Meter Freestyle Record

The third Jiangda Swimming Competition concluded yesterday. Jinan won the championship for the third consecutive year with a total of 25 points. Jiaotong came in second with 18 points, Fudan third with 14 points, Daxia fourth with 8 points, and Guanghua fifth with 1 point. Yu Rongbang of Jiaotong broke the Jiangda record of 30.9 seconds held by Lian Xiannan of Jinan in the 50-meter freestyle with a time of 30.2 seconds, making it one of the most exciting events of the competition. The other events did not show any progress. The women's group was changed to a performance due to only one or two participants. The scores of each school and the results of the finals are recorded below.

School Scores (1) Jinan University, 25 points, (2) Jiaotong University, 18 points, (3) Fudan University, 14 points, (4) Daxia University, 8 points, (5) Daguanghua University, 1 point,

Reasons for Jinan's Victory: Jinan's only strong opponent is Jiaotong. Their results in short-distance and backstroke are not as good as Jiaotong, ranking below them. The decision of victory or defeat lies entirely in the two long-distance events of 400 meters and 1500 meters, and Jinan's average talent takes the lead. There is talent in every event, and they score in every event. This is why they win.

Reasons for Jiaotong's Defeat: Jiaotong had a strong momentum to defeat Jinan and win the championship. They overwhelmed Jinan in the two short-distance events of 50 meters and 100 meters. Chen Chunxiu's 50 meters was particularly distinctive. Chen Hu's backstroke and breaststroke were also better than Jinan's. Unfortunately, they lack talent in the two events of 400 meters and 1500 meters, and have to let others take the high seat.

Tense Situation: The competition between Jinan and Jiaotong was the fiercest, with a very small difference in scores. After the 100-meter backstroke, each had 18 points. The last event, the 1500 meters, will decide the championship. However, looking back at Jiaotong, there is no talent in the final list. Therefore, Jinan can easily win.

A New Record: A new record was created yesterday. Yu Rongbang of Jiaotong broke the Jiangda record of 30.9 seconds held by Lian Xiannan of Jinan in the 50-meter freestyle with a time of 30.2 seconds.

Diving Performance: Results of the diving performance competition: (1) Chen Jiazhen of Jinan, (2) Bao Xindi of Jiaotong, (3) Pan Baozhen of Guanghua, (4) Li Linyan of Fudan.

Women's Performance: Because there was only one participant in the women's group, Liu Mali, it was changed to a performance. Ms. Liu Mali and Gong Xiji performed the 100-meter backstroke.

World Long-Distance Running Expert Nurmi's Amateur Status Question

International Athletic Association Cancels His Qualification

Finnish Athletic Association Claims No Violation

(London Dispatch) A very interesting question has arisen in the world of sports regarding Nurmi's status. Last year, the International Amateur Athletic Federation believed that Nurmi had violated amateur rules and was not allowed to participate in the Olympics. However, the strange thing is that Nurmi recently won the Finnish championship again. According to the Finnish Athletic Association, Nurmi has not violated any rules. Not only Nurmi personally believes that he is an amateur, but the Finnish Athletic Association also believes so. Therefore, he is allowed to compete in Finland. Nurmi has not left amateur sports, nor does he have any such intention. He continues to work hard to break world records and says that he does not run for money. As a result, such a special situation has arisen. Finland calls him an amateur, but the International Athletic Association cancels his qualification. According to the rules of the International Amateur Association, no amateur athletes may compete with him after Nurmi's qualification is canceled, nor may they compete with athletes who have competed with Nurmi.

Local News

Verification Period for Graduation Certificates from Colleges and Above

and Measures for Issuing Temporary Graduation Certificates

The Municipal Education Bureau Orders All Schools to Comply with the Ministry's Order

Education Bureau Instructions to Provincial and Registered Private Colleges and Above in this City, It is hereby ordered that, according to the Ministry of Education's Instruction No. 8374, after checking the graduation transcripts and graduation certificates of each graduating student from public and private colleges and above in the country, they must be submitted for record and verification within one month after the end of the semester. In January of the 20th year, Instruction No. 108 was issued for compliance. It is now found that many schools have not complied with the order to complete the procedures on time, and the issued temporary graduation certificates are unrestricted. It should be stipulated again as follows: Each school's graduation certificates for each graduating student must comply with the previous order and be submitted to the Ministry for verification within one month after the end of the semester. Late requests for supplementary verification will not be accepted. All graduation certificates that have not been verified will not be recognized by the Ministry. (2) Schools may not issue graduation certificates to students who have not passed the graduation examination. The graduation certificate for those who have passed the examination must have a student's photo affixed, be stamped with a steel seal, and indicate its validity period, which is limited to June. This certificate must be returned and canceled when exchanging for a formal graduation certificate. In addition to being distributed separately, the order is issued to the Bureau to instruct provincial or registered private colleges and above to strictly comply with the procedures. This order, etc., is hereby ordered to comply with the procedures. This order.

Zhang Yuanruo's Constitutional Theory

The entire book of 200,000 words will be published by the China Book Company-

Mr. Zhang Yuanruo, an expert in public law, has served as a law professor and dean of various universities. He has written extensively and is enthusiastic about academics. Recently, he has written a book on Chinese constitutionalism, totaling 200,000 words, which is broad and profound. It is divided into two parts, the first part is a general discussion of the characteristics of China's constitutionalism, the crux of constitutionalism, and the basic principles and special problems of future constitutional making. The second part discusses the latest principles of modern constitutional transformation and the latest trends in the evolution of modern constitutions. The second part is the main discussion, first discussing the general principles of constitutional making, and then discussing the basic principles of the rights and obligations of the people. The theory is detached from the traditional legal framework, and is especially aimed at the special circumstances of our country's plans. Then it discusses the central political system and the local system. It has unique contributions to the problems of the presidential system, the cabinet system, the committee system, the centralization of power, and the decentralization of power that have been disputed in our country for many years. Finally, it discusses the relationship between constitutional making and people's livelihood and the nation. It is incisive and novel, and is the highlight of this book. It has now been handed over to the China Book Company for printing and will be published soon. It is truly a great contribution to the academic community in our country in the voice of constitutional making.

Dawn of Production Education

Huangdu Chicken Farm to Expand

The China Education Construction Society and the Provincial Huangdu Rural Normal School jointly established the Huangdu Chicken Farm to promote education. It is located in Huangdu Town on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. It is learned that it has been in operation for more than half a year. The farm completely adopts scientific methods to hatch chicks. Great attention is paid to the air and temperature of the chicken house, the distribution and nutrition of feed, and the research and treatment of chicken diseases. On the one hand, it provides practical training for students of Huangdu Rural Normal School, and on the other hand, it recruits worker students in order to combine production and education. There are currently about 300 laying hens and dozens of breeding chickens. It is heard that the board of directors was held at the Li Da Academy in Jiangwan the other day. Directors Teng Songshi, Sun Yuanshu, Zhang Zhonghuan, Wu Zhiqian, Chen Ruiwen, and supervisors Zhou Linwu and Zhang Shiqiao attended. As a result of the discussion, it was decided to increase the capital in the spring of next year and expand the farm again. A report will be compiled and published to the society around Double Ten Day. It is also planned to borrow the New Bao Vocational School on Parker Road as a temporary liaison office in Shanghai. There are currently fat and tender roosters and large eggs for sale. It is heard that the Education Construction Society also plans to hold a general meeting of members in Huangdu after the Mid-Autumn Festival. It is expected that there will be a grand occasion at that time, and the farm will definitely make a great contribution to the future of production education.
